0618680004|5.0|Dawkins' God Delusion    \\"The God Delusion\\" by Richard Dawkins is a good read, worth the price, but its title is misleading. Dawkins' address is less about god and more about debunking the theism of the Abrahamic religions of Judaism, Christianity and Islam. His stated purpose is to convert his readership from such religions to atheism. As such, the book is Dawkins' latest salvo in his war against devout Western fundamentalism. By my reading, his arguments have merit and entertainment value and I expect many if not most readers will judge similarly. But I wonder if he's focusing on yesterday's battles to the detriment of more fundamental concerns.    Joseph Campbell, mythologist, has observed that humankind's god-belief is pervasive and the source of all religions. To deny its existence is to over-intellectualize the mysteries of existence. Each religion puts a face and symbology on the god-belief appropriate to its time, place and worldview, e.g. Zeus and his thunderbolts. When these elements change, a new face and symbology are required but the god-belief endures. Dawkins focuses on ancient faces and symbologies even as many in the modern world, including many of the devout, are searching for new faces and symbologies. Dawkins would maintain that such searchers have become atheistic, e.g. see his deism. [He is technically correct for deism but not strictly correct (for any religion) since all gods are potentially personal gods.] Others might suspect that those same searchers see themselves as evolving religiously. Dawkins ignores this possibility and appears to have limited awareness of the god-belief and its source, \\"The onus is not on me to answer.\\" (See middle pg. 270 to section end.) Perhaps with enough consciousness raising he could, to the profit of us all, redirect his iconoclastic energies and lead us to where the god-belief will take us next. Not likely, since shouldering this task might mean acknowledging the sense of the divine underlying much of what he calls atheism. Moreover, he would risk becoming a theologian, or worse a religious prophet, with his possible conversion from atheism to an evolved religion. Is Dawkins as the next Paul even imaginable?

B000GIXEIG|4.0|Not that there are many film versions of the Beowulf legend to choose from, but this recent adaptation by director Sturla Gunnarson is definitely worth a look.  Shot entirely on location in Iceland, this film offers a breathtaking look at the real world these characters would have inhabited.   <br /> <br />And that very reality is precisely what gives this film its power.  Gunnarson takes the story of Beowulf almost entirely out of the realm of myth and places it as close to reality as one might without removing it from all relevance.  Beowulf as a character is already dealing with his growing reputation as a hero and monster-slayer, yet he remains a human man who must deal with a perceived superhuman nemesis.  The treatment of the monster Grendel is rather unique and one can even interpret his depiction as a throwback to neanderthal man or some other precursor or subsect of homo-sapien evolution.  He is similar to a yeti or sasquatch, yet treated with dignity and allowed far more emotional depth and range than many would usually allow for such a creature. <br /> <br />Gunnarson obviously has been heavily influenced by John Gardner's Grendel, which retells the beowulf myth from the point of view of the monster.  Gunnarson remains as true to the story as possible considering the choices he makes in telling his version of the story. <br /> <br />The scenery of the film is nothing short of gorgeous and for those with a predisposition for the harsh stark landscapes of medieval Scandinavia this film will in no way disappoint.  The settings are kept minimal and efficient, as the cultures depicted would have practiced in reality.  There are no shining palaces of gold or massive castles on a hilltop.  This is not the Lord of the Rings.  It is however a truly magnificent movie about vikings and one of the rare few to boast such a mantle.   <br /> <br />The only other recent film which bears comparison is John McTiernan's 13th Warrior, based on the novel Eaters of the Dead byMichael Crichton.  That film is likewise a retelling of the Beowulf myth but it goes in a completely alternate direction and suffers greatly from a profound lack of historical accuracy despite its attempt to appear 'plausible.'   <br /> <br />The only questionable moments in Gunnarson's version are his depiction of the climactic fight between the hero and the monster (here it has been made deliberately anti-climactic) and also the way the relationships between Beowulf, the monster and the witch play out.   <br /> <br />Stellar performances are turned in by almost all members of the cast, especially Stellan SkarsgÃ¥rd as King Hrothgar and, of course, Gerard Butler as Beowulf himself.   <br /> <br />For those just interested in a slick medieval action/thriller, check ou the local video store and give this one a look.  For more serious fans of medieval legend/myth/folklore or especially avid buffs of the Beowulf legend itself, this one is worth the money. Buy it.

B000JK8OYU|3.0|I'll start by saying that I haven't seen the musical. That might make this product more meaningful, but no more than a typical soundtrack.    What you have with the CD is a montage of Beatles moments from their albums, singles, and even some of the Anthology series thrown in. Most songs appear in bits which come and go in a flash. Others are played out a little more, and a few get most of the way through in their original forms. It's a tapestry of Beatles moments all woven together--within, without--old and new mashed together. Almost a Beatles dream sequence.     The Beatles' original producer, George Martin and his son were the production team for this CD. From a production standpoint, it is fantastic. Their talent (as well as the quality of the tapes recorded long ago)really shines through. You must remember they were putting much of this together \\"made-to-order\\" to go with the vision of the \\"Love\\" muscial staff. The quality of most of the sound makes you long for a full remastering of the origingal Beatles albums using the same equipment. (Or how about the \\"Get Back\\" sessions in their entirety!)    But, unfortunately, there are some problems with this project. These problems are especially those which have to deal with efforts to make the Beatles appealing to fans of \\"the modern sound\\". Ringo's drums tying two songs together in perfect sync with the underlying beat takes us right into the modern club. However, \\"clubbing Beatles\\" just doesn't do it for me. (It's almost Silly Love Songs!) Another problem is that some of the songs seem really bass heavy. Get Back is totally ruined due to the pounding of the bass. My fifteen-year-old reached out and turned down the volume when it was on in my car. So much for appealing to the younger generation! (And I don't think the Beatles aim of getting back to their roots for the \\"Get Back/Let It Be\\" project included bass enhancement!)    Well, we have to remember that this is the soundtrack to the musical. But how little information is included about the stage presentation! What gives? We get a booklet of vague photographs, but that's about all.     So, we are left with the CD on its own, but why do we really want to listen to Beatles songs this way? When you put a mix CD or tape together, doesn't the fixed order get a little tiring? That's when you might hit the random button, but that won't work very well for this CD.    I can't imagine too many people listening to this CD more than about five times. I've talked with some others who feel the same way:    First listen: Cool! Very interesting!  Second listen: Oh, yeah. I like that part. (and) I didn't notice that the first time.  Third listen: Oh, yeah. That part.   Fourth listen: I feel like I've heard it all before. (and) Man, this thing goes on forever!  Fifth listen: ??? (There may not be a fifth listen.)    Well, maybe a dozen listens for some. But considering how new this CD is, and how many are already being sold used here at Amazon, I think quite a few people probably feel this way.     And when you really think about it, there are infinite arrangements that could be made from pieces of Beatle songs. It could be made into a series with hundreds of volumes! The individual tracks could even be sold in a software package and users could put their own mixes together. Dissected Beatles, Frankenstein Beatles...Wouldn't that be cool? But in the end, you have to ask yourself, \\"What's the point?\\" How many listens does it deserve?    But, if you're a true fan, like me, you know you have to have it. Just for the experience. For me, (for the first three times) the Mr. Kite/She's So Heavy blend/segue was a powerfully moving experience! But, now, like Let It Be Naked, it has been experienced.     As with all the other \\"post-Beatles\\" Beatles projects I own, \\"Love\\" has now been relegated to the \\"about once-a-year\\" rotation.

6304712936|5.0|This is my favorite movie of all time. It has less to do about the genius of Mozart than the genius of F. Murray Abraham, who delivers one of the finest acting I have ever seen. Abraham plays the role of Antonio Salieri, who had been promoted to the rank of kapellmeister (chief Royal music-maker) in the Vienna court of the late 18th century.<br /><br />The movie begins with an attempted suicide of Salieri. His unsuccessful attempt to die is followed by his residence in an asylum, where a piano is also furnished for his enjoyment. The story really begins when a priest visits Salieri to listen what the latter has to say and bring some comfort to his misery. Alas, Salieri's misery hardly subsides when the priest fails to recognize any of Salieri's works as the deranged man plays melody after melody, which were once \\"the joy of Vienna\\". Oh but wait, he says, how about this one. Unbeknownst to the priest Salieri plays a simple melody familiar to both the man of God and the person watching the movie. Oh that's charming! exclaims the priest. I didn't know you wrote that, says the priest with new found respect for the ill man. And the introduction to the story ends when Salieri says: I didn't. That was Mozart.<br /><br />The story flows with the transformation of Salieri's character. From his innocent childhood to an ambitious career-oriented musician, whose sole purpose in life is his music and he works very hard to be recognized for it. But Nature works in mysterious ways. It humbles hard workers by showing there is always someone better. So much better in fact humility turns to mediocrity and sometimes into raging jealousy, and so the seeds of a story are sowed.
1592401791|5.0|If you'd like to see why Geoff Emerick is important, pull out your copy of Revolver, and then a couple of other CDs by the Beatles's mid-60s crosstown rivals, like the Who or the Stones.  Listen on headphones.  Notice the difference?  Like, on the Beatles album, you can actually hear the bass guitar?  Emerick was part of a crack team at EMI, headed by George Martin, who produced these groundbreaking sounds using technology based in vacuum tubes and scissors.<br /><br />As a serious Beatlemaniac, I was excited to hear Emerick's take on things.  I've read a fair selection of books about the Fabs, ranging from Lewisohn's obsessive documentation of their recording sessions to Goldman's ridiculous Lennon bio.  Here, There and Everywhere might just be the best of the lot.<br /><br />Emerick had not only privileged access to the boys at work during some seminal album sessions, he also has the rare gift of seeing them as actual human beings, with all the flashes of brilliance rounded by a dash of annoying quirks.  He was so stung by one of Lennon's barbs that he actually walked out on recording the White Album (imagine!), but nonetheless admires John's genius, and even credits Yoko where he thinks credit is due.<br /><br />Smart anecdotes abound.  One I found most striking was Yoko, recovering from a car crash, holding her own personal bed-in inside the studio during the recording of Abby Road.  Ah, I miss the 60s!<br /><br />There's also a bit of technical information (Emerick is, after all, an engineer), but don't be intimidated.  As Elvis Costello comments in his gracious introduction, most of the stories seem to involve a charming jury-rigged MacGyver-style solution involving sticky tape and rubber bands.  Many of the best involve the professional musicians who interacted with the Beatles for various recordings--they were reluctant to turn down what was definitely the best gig in England, but nevertheless disconcerted by the men sticking microphones in their faces and persuading them to play wearing pig noses.<br /><br />One note of caution:  before you start reading, make sure you have your CDs as well as your Anthology DVDs nearby--you'll definitely want to grab everything and give it a new listen.faces and persuading them to play wearing pig noses. <br /> <br />One note of caution:  before you start reading, make sure you have your CDs as well as your Anthology DVDs nearby--you'll definitely want to grab everything and give it a new listen.

0743270754|5.0|Doris Kearns Goodwin has added an important element to our understanding of Lincoln.  This a biography not just of one of our greatest presidents but of the politicians and administrators who were part of his cabinet, the Congress and his official family while he was in the White House.  She deftly illustrates Lincoln's \\"political genius\\" -- his ability to bind men who had run against him for president or otherwise opposed him by incorporating them into his cabinet and/or administration and earning first their respect and then their affection.  His brilliance and his extraordinary patience and generosity have never been more clearly illustrated. If a Bob Woodward or Frank Rich had written about Lincoln in the 1860s, this is probably the kind of insight readers would have had.

B000KX0HVY|4.0|Without question, Elvis has been the most anthologized artist in the nearly thirty years since his death. So how is this collection different from the others? The short answer is--nothing. If you're a die-hard fan, there's no reason to buy this.  But that's not true for the casual fan who's looking for a comprehensive overview of perhaps the most influential performer of the 20th Century.<br /><br />This mid-priced two-disc collection covers every aspects of Elvis's career, beginning with his first Sun single \\"That's All Right\\" through the 1977 single \\"Moody Blue,\\" which topped the country chart just months before his death. In between are hits from every stage of his career--50's rock 'n' roll classics like \\"Hound Dog,\\" movie hits like the million-seller \\"Viva Las Vegas\\" and comeback hits like \\"Suspicious Minds\\" (his first No. 1 in more than seven years!).<br /><br />Sure, there are missing tracks (including nine No. 1's, like \\"(Let Me Be Your)Teddy Bear,\\" \\"Stuck on You\\" and \\"Good Luck Charm\\"), but for the casual fan who only wants one anthology in their collection this works nicely. However, with a total playing time of less than two hours, it could have been more inclusive.  HIGHLY RECOMMENDED

Only in her last and apparently semi-autbiographical novel, Persuasion, does one get a sense of the depth of her regrets and the pathos of her short life. B0007Y08IS|1.0|I guess it helps if one is a \\"South Park\\" fan.  I've never been.<br /><br />Still, I was ready to give this every chance in the world to make a comedic, satrical, sarcastic, perceptive socio-political take on our modern times, even with cheap production values, even cheaper looking puppets, and little if no imagination or funny jokes from the beginning 10-15 minutes.  As this film ain't no 4 hour deal, finding nothing remotely interesting, let alone humorous or clever in the first quarter or fifth, I was amazed how just plain unimaginative and boring this was.<br /><br />A film has to be really bad from the beginning for me to start fast forwarding within the first 20 minutes.  Usually by that time, I'm either willing to stick it out, or just give up.  This movie had neither quality.  By 20 minutes, my mind had thought of a hundred or so better uses of my time than this.  I skipped ahead only to find that to the end, there was no real brain food here.<br /><br />While South Park has (deservedly so or not) a reputation for taking real chances, why I asked, was this all so lame?  Was it just the crap visuals, the various flat jokes, or something much deeper?  For while neo-libs have embraced South Park the TV series for its innovations and anti-establishment ramblings, while this movie seems a big screen attempt at the same, the corporate influence and underlying neo-con truth of the South Park folks takes over.  A quick buck.  Capitalism at its worst.  In movie form.  Yee-hah.  Blah...<br /><br />What's most disturbing is that while this is supposedly supposed to be an indictment of sorts of blind patriotic American zeal and over-indulgence and arrogance, it ends up strangely justifying that very premise, and promoting it.  And while there is an overall criticism of recent US foreign policy, the \\"bad guys\\" still end up the same old \\"bad guys\\" as official US corporate media has sold us all along.  This makes the whole exercise lack not only sarcasm and satire, but right-on humor as well.<br /><br />I had looked forward to seeing this, even though I hate South Park.  I had hoped that those folks would really let loose here, and the shame is that most people who'll end up liking this, will like it only for its South Park connections, but not for what the movie really is, or is all about.<br /><br />A lot I'd bet will even take the final messages this delivers as somehow validating their faith in their seemingly leftist ideals.  The disappointing thing is that it does the exact opposite.  The creators of this obviously do not understand exactly what they're trying to present except to try to cash in on South Park trendy anti-establishment underpinnings.  Then again, I never thought South Park the series did (or does) that either.<br /><br />The only decent thing about this bore-fest is a few slightly humorous self-referential PUPPET jokes.  Otherwise, it is not visually compelling or innovative, most of the humor and the social and political elements tend towards the far right view of modern day reality, and one mostly fast-forwarded viewing of this was enough for me to dismiss this as nothing more than a wasted use of some seemingly real talent here and there.<br /><br />Again, as in most bad movies, the problem here is the writing.  I guess if you can get through the first 20 minutes or so without your mind wandering, you might get through the rest, then put watching this over again off for another decade.  I can't imagine any but a die hard and rich DVD collector actually wanting to own this.  It's basically just plain boring, what else can I say?<br /><br />I wonder if the puppet presentation was cheaper than a decent animated and CGI rendering, and if so, there's another problem. This is cheap schlock which doesn't even seem to understand or comprehend its own preachings, and done seemingly on a shoestring budget.  This film never goes far enough, never.  It was evident in the first 15-20 minutes, and the disappointment throughout only reinforces that.<br /><br />I wouldn't buy this at any price.  I wouldn't even want it free.  It's bad and boring from beginning to end.  There may be a short 10-15 South Park film here.  Stretched out to feature length, it is a way overlong and unenlightening, unfunny waste of time.isappointment throughout only reinforces that. <br /> <br />I wouldn't buy this at any price.
